(K.) The Koofees hold it to be in the acc. case as an adv. n. of place: the Basrees, as an inf. n., in every instance; as though thou saidst <foreign lang="ar">أَوْحَدْتُهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بِرُؤْيَتِى إِبحَادًا</foreign>, meaning “ I saw none save him, ” and then substituted <foreign lang="ar">وحده</foreign>: or, as Abu-l-'Abbás says, it may mean the man's being himself alone; as though thou saidst <foreign lang="ar">رَأَيْتُ رَجُلًا مُنْفَرِدًا</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">اِنْفِرَادًا</foreign>, and then substituted <foreign lang="ar">وحده</foreign>. (S.) Or it is in the acc. case as a denotative of state accord. to the Basrees [and the grammarians in general]; not as an inf. n., J being in error in what he says on this matter: (IB, K:) the Basrees hold it to be a noun occupying the place of an inf. n. in the acc. case as a denotative of state; like <foreign lang="ar">جَآءَ زَيْدٌ رَكْضًا</foreign>, meaning <foreign lang="ar">رَاكِضًا</foreign>: (IB:) excepting some of them, as Yoo, who holds it to be in the acc. case as an adv. n. of place, for <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى وَحْدِهِ</foreign>, (IB, K,) like <foreign lang="ar">عِنْدَهُ</foreign>: (TA:) and there is a third opinion, that of Hishám; that it is in the acc. case as an inf. n. (L.) Or, (accord. to IAar, L,) it is a noun used as a noun absolutely: (L, K:) so in the dial. of the Benoo-Temeem: (Msb:) you say <foreign lang="ar">جَلَسَ وَحْدَهُ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى وَحْدِهِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">جَلَسَا عَلَى وَحْدِ هِمَا</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">وَحْدَيْهِمَا</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">جَلَسُوا عَلَى وَحْدِهِمْ</foreign>, [<hi rend="ital">He sat alone,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">they two sat alone,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">they sat alone</hi>]. (L, K.) When not preceded by a prefixed n. [or a prep.], it is always in the acc. case: (Lth, L:) you say, <foreign lang="ar">لَا إِلَاَه إِلَّا ٱللّٰهُ وَحْدَهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">There is no deity but God alone</hi>]: and <foreign lang="ar">مَرَرْتُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بِزَيْدٍ وَحْدَهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I passed by Zeyd alone</hi>]: (L:) [excepting in a few cases, such as the phrases] <foreign lang="ar">قُلْنَا هٰذَا الأَمْرَ وَحْدَيْنَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">We two alone said this thing</hi>], and <foreign lang="ar">قَالَتَاهُ وَحْدَيْهُمَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">They two</hi> women <hi rend="ital">alone said it</hi>]; mentioned by AZ. (L.) You say also, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا عَلَى وَحْدِهِ</foreign>, and   
      <foreign lang="ar">عَلَى <ref cref="n41734-1" target="حِدَتِهِ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, <hi rend="ital">This is by itself;</hi> (L, K;) and <foreign lang="ar">هُمَا عَلَى حِدَتِهِمَا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">They two are by themselves:</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">هُمْ عَلَى حِدَتِهِمْ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">They are by themselves:</hi> (L:) and <foreign lang="ar">أَعْطِ كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مَنْهُمْ عَلَى حِدَتِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Give thou to every one of them by himself;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">على حِيَالِهِ</foreign>. (S.) The <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign> in <foreign lang="ar">حِدَةٌ</foreign> is a substitute for the <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> (S, L) which is cut off from the beginning. (L.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">وَحْدٌ</foreign>, (K,) or   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n41734-2" target="وَحَدٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n41735"/></foreign>, (L,) A wild animal <hi rend="ital">alone, by itself,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">apart from others.</hi> (L, K.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">وَحَدٌ</foreign>, (K,) or   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n41734-3" target="وَحَدٌ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n41735"/></foreign>, (L,) A man <hi rend="ital">whose lineage and origin are unknown.</hi> (Lth, L, K.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">وَحْد</foreign> is used as the complement of a prefixed n. only in the following phrases: (A'Obeyd, S, L:) <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ نَسِيجُ وَحْدِهِ</foreign>, which is an expression of praise; (S, L, K;) meaning, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">He is one unequalled; one who has no second:</hi> (L:) or <hi rend="ital">he is a man of right judgment:</hi> you say also <foreign lang="ar">هُمَا نَسِيجَا وَحْدِهِمَا</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">هُمْ نُسَجَآءُ وَحْدِهِمْ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">هِىَ نَسِيجَةُ وَحْدِهَا</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">هُنَّ نَسَائِجُ وَحْدِهِنَّ</foreign>: (Lth, L:) [see art. <foreign lang="ar">نسج</foreign>:] it is as though you said <foreign lang="ar">نَسِيجُ إِفْرَادٍ</foreign>: you put <foreign lang="ar">وحده</foreign> in the place of an inf. n. in the gen. case: (S:) and <foreign lang="ar">رَجُلُ وَحْدِهِ</foreign>, (IAar, L,) and <foreign lang="ar">رُجَيْلُ وَحْدِهِ</foreign>, (S, L,) [<hi rend="ital">A man unequalled; who has no second,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">a little man</hi> (probably meaning the contr.) &amp;c.]: and <foreign lang="ar">قَرِيعُ وَحْدِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">A man with whom no one contends in excellence:</hi> (Lth, L:) and <foreign lang="ar">عُيَيْرُ وَحْدِهِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">جُحَيْشُ وَحْدِهِ</foreign>, which are expressions of dispraise; (S, L, K;) meaning, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">One who does not consult, nor mix with, any one, and who is contemptible and weak:</hi> (Sh, L:) <foreign lang="ar">وَحْد</foreign> being used in the manner of an inf. n., not being an epithet nor an enunciative so as to be in concordance with the preceding noun, would be more properly in the acc. case; but the Arabs use it in these instances as the complement of a prefixed n.: (Lth, L:) these expressions are indeterminate: for the Arabs say, <foreign lang="ar">رُبَّ نَسِيجِ وَحْدِهِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">قَدْ رَأَيْتُ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">Few unequalled men have I seen</hi>]. (Hishám, Fr., L.)    </entryFree>2a:T452,<entryFree id="n41737" key="وَحْدَةٌ" type="main">

                  </form> The <hi rend="ital">state of being alone,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">apart from others; solitariness; solitude.</hi> (Sb, S.)                   <hi rend="ital">The night of solitude;</hi> the first night after burial: so called because the soul is believed to remain in the grave during this night, and then to depart to the place appointed for the residence of good souls until the last day, or to the appointed prison in which wicked souls await their final doom.                   <hi rend="ital">One;</hi> the <hi rend="ital">first of the numbers:</hi> (S, L, Msb, K:) syn. [in many cases, which will be shown below,] with <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدٌ</foreign>: (K:) [and <hi rend="ital">one alone:</hi> a <hi rend="ital">single</hi> person or thing:] fem. <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدَةٌ</foreign>: (L, Msb:) it sometimes receives the dual form; (L, K;) as in the expression <foreign lang="ar">إِلْتَقَيْنَا وَاحِدَيْنِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">We met, we being each of us one alone</hi>]; cited from a poet by IAar: or the dual form pertains to it in another sense, explained below, namely “ alone: ” (L:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدُونَ</foreign> (S, L, K) and <foreign lang="ar">وُحْدَانٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أُحْدَانٌ</foreign>; (S, L;) in the last of which, <foreign lang="ar">أ</foreign> is substituted for <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> because of the dammeh: (L:) one says, <foreign lang="ar">أَنْتُمْ حَىٌّ وَاحِدٌ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">حَىٌّ وَاحِدُونَ</foreign>, (Ye are one tribe, L) like as one says <foreign lang="ar">شِرْذِمَةٌ قَلِيلُونَ</foreign>: (Fr, S, L:) <foreign lang="ar">آحَادٌ</foreign> may also be a pl. of <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدٌ</foreign> [and therefore originally <foreign lang="ar">أَوْحَادٌ</foreign>,] like as <foreign lang="ar">أَشْهَادٌ</foreign> is pl. of <foreign lang="ar">شَاهِدٌ</foreign>. (Th, Msb.) Its proper signification is A thing <hi rend="ital">having no subdivision:</hi> and it is secondarily applied to any existing thing; so that there is no number to which it may not be applied as an epithet; wherefore one says, <foreign lang="ar">عَشَرَةٌ وَاحِدَةٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">One ten</hi>], and <foreign lang="ar">مِائَةٌ وَاحِدَةٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">One hundred</hi>]. (Er-Rághib.) It is interchangeable for <foreign lang="ar">أَحَدٌ</foreign> when used as an epithet applied to God; and in certain nouns of number. [See art. <foreign lang="ar">أحد</foreign>.] In most cases differing from these two, there is a difference in usage. The latter is used in affirmative phrases as a prefixed noun only, governing the noun which follows it in the gen. case; and is used absolutely in negative phrases: whereas the former is used in affirmative phrases as a prefixed n. and otherwise. (Msb.) [See, again, art. <foreign lang="ar">أَحد</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>

                  <hi rend="ital">I am not alone, without a parallel,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">watch, in this affair:</hi> (S, * L, K: *) or simply, <hi rend="ital">I am not alone in it.</hi> (T, L.)                   </form> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n41747-1" target="وُحَادَ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n41740"/></foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">أُحَادَ</foreign> [used adverbially] are imperfectly decl. because of their having the quality of an epithet and deviating from their original form, (S, L,) which is <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدًا</foreign>: (L, K:) or because they differ from their original both as to the letter and the meaning; the original word being changed as above stated, and the meaning being changed to <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدًا وَاحِدًا</foreign>: (S, L:) you say <foreign lang="ar">دَخَلُوا مَوْحَدَ مَوْحَدَ</foreign>, (S, L, K,) [and <foreign lang="ar">وُحَادَ وُحَادَ</foreign>,] and <foreign lang="ar">أُحَادَ أُحَادَ</foreign>, (L, K,) <hi rend="ital">They entered one</hi> [<hi rend="ital">and</hi>] <hi rend="ital">one,</hi> [<hi rend="ital">one and one</hi>]; or <hi rend="ital">one</hi> [<hi rend="ital">by</hi>] <hi rend="ital">one,</hi> [<hi rend="ital">one by one</hi>]; (K;) or <hi rend="ital">one at a time; one after another.</hi> (S, L.)    </entryFree>2e:T5d5,<entryFree id="n41749" key="مِيحَادٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">مِيحَادٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> 
                  <hi rend="ital">One of several hills, such as are called</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَكَمَات</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">separate</hi> or <hi rend="ital">remote, one from another:</hi> pl. <foreign lang="ar">مَوَاحِيدُ</foreign>. (L, K.) F remarks, that J is in error in saying, <foreign lang="ar">المِيحَادُ مِنَ الوَاحِدِ كَالمِعْشَارِ مِنَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">العَشَرَةِ</foreign>: (TA:) but the meaning of this is, that it denotes <hi rend="ital">one part</hi> or <hi rend="ital">portion;</hi> like as <foreign lang="ar">مِعْشَارٌ</foreign> signifies one of ten: (L:) [i. e., the former signifies <hi rend="ital">one of several things whereof each is alone,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by itself:</hi>] and the same explanation is given by [several] old authors. (TA.) [In one copy of the S, instead of <foreign lang="ar">العَشَرَة</foreign>, I find <foreign lang="ar">العُشْر</foreign>; which affords a good sense, i. e., that <foreign lang="ar">ميحاد</foreign>, is syn. with <foreign lang="ar">وَاحِدٌ</foreign>; and may be the true reading.]
